  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2e6c0158-a93e-48eb-97c4-20f577317b2b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2710603987510642932"><b>Every enchantment has a price.</b><br/><br/>With a flick of her paintbrush, Isobel creates stunning portraits for a dangerous set of clients: the fair folk. These immortal creatures cannot bake bread or put a pen to paper without crumbling to dust. They crave human Craft with a terrible thirst, and they trade valuable enchantments for Isobel’s paintings. But when she receives her first </span>
  <span id="freeText2710603987510642932" style="display:none"><b>Every enchantment has a price.</b><br /><br />With a flick of her paintbrush, Isobel creates stunning portraits for a dangerous set of clients: the fair folk. These immortal creatures cannot bake bread or put a pen to paper without crumbling to dust. They crave human Craft with a terrible thirst, and they trade valuable enchantments for Isobel’s paintings. But when she receives her first royal patron—Rook, the autumn prince—Isobel makes a deadly mistake. She paints mortal sorrow in his eyes, a weakness that could cost him his throne, and even his life.<br /><br />Furious, Rook spirits Isobel away to his kingdom to stand trial for her crime. But something is seriously amiss in his world, and they are attacked from every side. With Isobel and Rook depending upon each other for survival, their alliance blossoms into trust, perhaps even love . . . a forbidden emotion that would violate the fair folks’ ruthless laws, rendering both their lives forfeit. What force could Isobel's paintings conjure that is powerful enough to defy the ancient malice of the fairy courts?<br /><br />Isobel and Rook journey along a knife-edge in a lush world where beauty masks corruption and the cost of survival might be more frightening than death itself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2710603987510642932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1977427343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13612763969446580114"><blockquote>
  <i>This wasn't like me. So many years of being cautious, and in a matter of minutes I'd started slipping up.</i>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens' title='An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Enchantment of Ravens</a> is not badly-written, but it is definitely not a book for me. I really wish I'd read some reviews before starting it and noted the comparison to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_' title='A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>. <b>ACOTAR fans should love this</b>.<br/><br/>This book is for fans of that particular brand of YA romance where a smart, level-headed young woman meets (and is kidnapped by) a prince and her brain instantly t</span>
  <span id="freeText13612763969446580114" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>This wasn't like me. So many years of being cautious, and in a matter of minutes I'd started slipping up.</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens" title="An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens</a> is not badly-written, but it is definitely not a book for me. I really wish I'd read some reviews before starting it and noted the comparison to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>. <b>ACOTAR fans should love this</b>.<br /><br />This book is for fans of that particular brand of YA romance where a smart, level-headed young woman meets (and is kidnapped by) a prince and her brain instantly turns to mush. My initial liking for Isobel quickly turned sour as she threw sense to the wind and started going all googly-eyed over a fae prince <b>she has known for about five minutes</b>. Declarations of love come about halfway through, but it is clear where the story is headed almost instantly.<br /><br />Isobel is a portrait artist and the number one choice for fair folk looking to bask in their vanity and enjoy the experience of human Craft for a while. Though immortal, the fae cannot create any kind of art without turning to dust, so Isobel's work is very popular among them. Then she finds herself with a very special client - the autumn prince, AKA Rook - and everything changes.<br /><br />Isobel paints human sorrow into Rook's eyes, therefore humiliating him in front of his fellow fae. He returns, takes her prisoner, and they start trekking through the fairy lands to the autumn court where Isobel will stand trial for her crime. <br /><br />I wasn't expecting this to be a <b>journey book</b> and probably wouldn't have picked it if I'd known. There are a few exceptions but, in general, I'm not a fan of books where most of the plot consists of the characters travelling from one place to another. And is it just me or does the reasoning all seem a bit... lame? Rook’s reputation is ruined because she paints human sorrow in his eyes? Yeah right. More like <b>an excuse was needed to get the two of them to go road-tripping together</b> - and give Rook the opportunity to take his shirt off and to save Isobel multiple times. <br /><br />I was expecting something more from this. Some more magic, more political intrigue, more relationships beyond the central love story... but it is sadly little more than a <b>predictable romance</b>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13612763969446580114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1903295941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903295941" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1903295941?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-couples">favorite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=arcs-i-ve-reviewed">arcs-i-ve-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1903295941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15115438083015791755"><b>Margaret Rogerson was born to write.</b><br/><br/>This was my most anticipated novel of the year, and I nearly cried when it showed up on my doorstep. So first and foremost, thank you, Simon and Schuster, for sending me a gorgeous physical copy that I will take 10 billion photos of. <br/><br/>This is the type of story that leaves an impression on you. If you're a writer, have a notebook handy, because you're going to want to highlight or jot down literally HALF this book because the language and prose are that gorgeous</span>
  <span id="freeText15115438083015791755" style="display:none"><b>Margaret Rogerson was born to write.</b><br /><br />This was my most anticipated novel of the year, and I nearly cried when it showed up on my doorstep. So first and foremost, thank you, Simon and Schuster, for sending me a gorgeous physical copy that I will take 10 billion photos of. <br /><br />This is the type of story that leaves an impression on you. If you're a writer, have a notebook handy, because you're going to want to highlight or jot down literally HALF this book because the language and prose are that gorgeous. I'm not joking when I say this is absolutely hands down the most beautiful book I've read.<br /><br />I don't say that lightly. I want SO BADLY to share so many quotes with you all in this review but since it was an ARC, I feel that I should wait a little longer. UGH.<br /><br />That being said, If you have any love for original fairy folklore, this book is for you. It holds true to so much existing folklore, but at the same time, it is totally unique and a free breath of air. The plot is completely unpredictable, in my opinion, and while it was in majority a traveling book, the adventure aspect had me totally hooked. I also found myself laughing out loud at several bits - like okay.. the fairies have to be proper or they get all freaked out. You'll see what I mean. It's great.<br /><br />Isobel is an artist. Let's pause there. Holy wow did Margaret research her art terms. That, or she must be one herself. She described (perfectly) everything from making paint/pigments from scratch to blending colors in ways that most writers would miss.<br /><br />Alright, alright. Moving on... Isobel paints portraits for the fairy folk, because since they aren't able to do craft (i.e. cooking, painting, writing...) themselves, they are quite taken by it and collect any human craft work they can get their hands on. Isobel, being the clever girl she is, has found a way to trade her portraits for enchantments that make her farm life easier. <br /><br />One particular fairy, who I won't spoil yet, tends to keep coming back to her for more and more portraits and in return, he helps her with such. (I ended up loving this character as much as I loved Rook because UGH so much sass, I love him. *whispers into the void...Can he please have his own book?* ) <br /><br />And then one day, said fairy is all like 'Oh by the by... the Autumn prince is gonna show up tomorrow and you're going to paint his picture OK BYE.'<br /><br />So Isobel freaks out. I would too.<br /><br />Anyway, said prince shows up in a SUPER COOL WAY that I will not spoil, and as you can tell from the synopsis, his name is Rook. And he's adorable. I literally cannot.<br /><br />I don't want to say much more aside from what you can glean from the synopsis because let's face it, the book is too good to spoil, but in short - faeries don't have 'emotions' save for love really... and that's even rare. Isobel sees a sorrow in Rook though and dares to paint it on his face. When Rook receives the final painting, he's pissed, because sorrow makes him look weak. He drags Isobel from her home and whisks her off to fairyland to 'stand trial'. <br /><br />But the journey is nothing like they imagine.<br /><br />All in all, every minute of this is breathtaking, heart-wrenching, and you won't want to leave this world. My only complaint is I feel like there were too many loose ends (and the ending felt a little rushed) so as I read the last page, I was like... what? There has to be more, right? <br /><br />So my hope is that Margaret plans to write us 9023032984234 more books. And at LEAST one more in this world following Rook and Isobel. That being said, she totally got me. While I did see the plot twist about *someone* coming, I did NOT see the ending coming. Holy crap. So like, I loved it, but I was also like... what? I NEED MORE....<br /><br />Ps... I drew a hand-lettered quote that you can get via my Etsy, linked below! <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15115438083015791755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2861568657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2861568657" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2861568657?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=uppercase">uppercase</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2861568657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15736731532281370223">4.5 stars <blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561919944i/27747649._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote>Before I begin, just letting you know that I got my copy from <a href='https://www.uppercasebox.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uppercase</a> - a lovely monthly book subscription box.<br/><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561919944i/27747650._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote>It was so exciting to read a book that the author signed!! <blockquote>
  <i>I was alive in a way I never had been before, in a world that no longer felt stale but instead crackled with breathless promise.</i>
</blockquote><b> Isobel lives in Whimsy,</b> a little pocket of fairyland, along with her aunt and March and May, her twin ex-goat siblings (ex-goat because...well... they used to be the family's goats </span>
  <span id="freeText15736731532281370223" style="display:none">4.5 stars <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561919944i/27747649._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>Before I begin, just letting you know that I got my copy from <a href="https://www.uppercasebox.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Uppercase</a> - a lovely monthly book subscription box.<br><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561919944i/27747650._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote>It was so exciting to read a book that the author signed!! <blockquote>
  <i>I was alive in a way I never had been before, in a world that no longer felt stale but instead crackled with breathless promise.</i>
</blockquote><b> Isobel lives in Whimsy,</b> a little pocket of fairyland, along with her aunt and March and May, her twin ex-goat siblings (ex-goat because...well... they used to be the family's goats until a fairy decided that they'd be more fun as humans) .<br><b><br>Fairies are hungry creatures </b>- anything from freshly baked bread to stunning works of art. They devour it all but they cannot lift a finger to do it themselves without crumbling to dust.<br><br>Isobel is a portrait artist of the immortals and she know <b>she is in a precarious position</b> - a wrong flick of her brush could irrevocably offend the fair folk.<blockquote>
  <i>Walking along a blade’s edge was only fun until the blade stopped being a metaphor.</i>
</blockquote>The autumn prince, Rook, desires a painting and Isobel obliges but adds an unexpected touch. She sees a flicker of sorrow on the prince's face and on an impulse adds it in.<blockquote>
  <i>This wasn't like me. So many years of being cautious, and in a matter of minutes I'd started slipping up.</i>
</blockquote><b>
  <u>Wrong. Move. </u>
</b><br><br>Little does Isobel know, any form of weakness - especially human emotion - marks the autumnal prince as a target. <br><br>So, Rook does the logical thing and <b>kidnaps her to stand trial for her crimes. </b><br><br>But the journey to the Autumnlands is treacherous and the stakes are high. <br><br>The<b> Alder King is awakening</b> and the Wild Hunt's hounds are snapping at their heels.<br><br>Soon, Isobel will learn that the only thing worse than a fairy feeling an emotion is when the fairy falls in love.<blockquote>
  <i>Why do we desire, above all other things, that which has the greatest power to destroy us?</i>
</blockquote>I was very impressed!<br><br> This totally feels like<b> a non-edgy Holly Black</b> (am I the only one?). I love Holly Black for her intensity but now I'm going to have to watch Margaret Rogerson for her whimsy. <br><br>The world Rogerson created blew me away. <br><br>Her interpretation of the fair folk - with all their<b> weird quirks and cruel intentions</b> - brought them completely to life.<blockquote>
  <i>...all around me sat empty people in rotting clothes, nibbling on flyblown trifles while they spoke of nothing of consequence with fixed smiles on their false faces.</i>
</blockquote>I adored all of the small details thrown in - especially how Isobel chose payment for her craft, often choosing the most mundane of enchantments. <blockquote>
  <i>"You are the most admired Crafter of thus age...and yet you request eggs."<br><br>“I quite like eggs,” I replied firmly, well aware that the enchantments he described would all turn strange and sour, even deadly, in the end.</i>
</blockquote>All those little bits completely drew me into the story.<br><b><br>I even (mostly) enjoyed the love story</b>, though it did tread on some of my biggest pet peeves - over-the-top instalove.<br><br>( It bugs me when characters spend less than a week together an suddenly it's love. )<blockquote>
  <i>Isobel, I love you wholly. I love you eternally. I love you so dearly it frightens me. I fear I could not live without you. I could see your face every morning upon waking for a thousand years and still look forward to the next as though it were the first.</i>
</blockquote> <b>It's just like, calm down already. <u>Keep the pants on.</u></b><br><br>Other than that, I really did enjoy my time with this novel! <b>Definitely an author to watch!!</b><blockquote>
  <i>Ah, but you were not a pawn. All along, you have been the queen.</i>
</blockquote><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Julia Whelan and wow - she did a fabulous job. Her tone and pitch was just completely perfect. Loved this listen!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_2114291193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2114291193" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2114291193?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481497596" href="/book/show/38472041-an-enchantment-of-ravens">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2114291193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17013714176698051261">This book was the ultimate comfort food for me with its lush prose, soft characters, and romantic fluff. The protagonist is down-to-earth, practical, and sweet, the love interest is endearingly arrogant, and the world is the most whimsical, atmospheric version of autumn. A common criticism seems to be that this is a very average fairy tale, but I actually really enjoyed the quiet simplicity of the narrative. This is not a drawn-out five-book series. It doesn’t try to be anything grander than it </span>
  <span id="freeText17013714176698051261" style="display:none">This book was the ultimate comfort food for me with its lush prose, soft characters, and romantic fluff. The protagonist is down-to-earth, practical, and sweet, the love interest is endearingly arrogant, and the world is the most whimsical, atmospheric version of autumn. A common criticism seems to be that this is a very average fairy tale, but I actually really enjoyed the quiet simplicity of the narrative. This is not a drawn-out five-book series. It doesn’t try to be anything grander than it is. It’s a simple, nice, magical love story, and it’s freaking cute, so screw it, I’m giving it 5 stars. My only criticism is that I need more fluff. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17013714176698051261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2040570555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2040570555" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2040570555?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2040570555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7115047798097608863"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500080274i/23296638._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Simon & Schuster in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You are like a living rose among wax flowers. We maybe last forever, but you bloom brighter and smell sweeter, and draw blood with your thorns.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Let me preface this review by letting you all know that all I want in this life is to read books about the fae. Seriously, give me a rainy or snowy day, a big hot cup of tea or coffee, and a book involving anything to do with faeries and I'll be a happy woman. I was completely</span>
  <span id="freeText7115047798097608863" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500080274i/23296638._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Simon &amp; Schuster in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You are like a living rose among wax flowers. We maybe last forever, but you bloom brighter and smell sweeter, and draw blood with your thorns.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Let me preface this review by letting you all know that all I want in this life is to read books about the fae. Seriously, give me a rainy or snowy day, a big hot cup of tea or coffee, and a book involving anything to do with faeries and I'll be a happy woman. I was completely captivated and entirely immersed in Margaret Rogerson's debut novel, <i>An Enchantment of Ravens</i>.<br><br>This story is about a young human girl, Isobel, who is from a city, Whimsy, which lives in a constant state of summer. She is a very talented painter, who focuses on portraits for fair folk subjects from the fairy courts, and in return they grant her different enchantments. But she has to make sure the wording is precise, because the fae in this book are rather mischievous creatures that excel in trickery. <br><br>Isobel is very well known by the fae for her painting Craft. See, in this world, even though the fair folk are magical and immortal beings, they are unable to ever create. This means painting, drawing, writing, even tasks like cooking. And Isobel is the most talented and beloved painter among the fair folk. She has many regular fair folk clients, but her world completely changes when she gets a much unexpected message that she will soon be painting the prince of the autumn court, Rook. Isobel gladly accepts, but makes the deadly mistake of painting exactly what she sees, which is mortal sorrow in his eyes.<br><br>This simple and overlooked minor detail ends up making Rook look weak and all the fair folk to look down upon him. Rook then rushes back to Whimsy to collect Isobel herself, and together they embark on an adventure to right the wrong of painting human emotion on a fair folk that is supposed to feel nothing. That is, until Isobel and Rook start to develop stronger feelings for one another and they break the Good Law that the Adler King set in place, which states that a fair folk and a human can never love one another and that it will be punishable with death. <br><br>Besides Isobel trying to correct painting the emotion, while also trying to keep her emotions in control, we have the Wild Hunt that has fae beasts constantly after them, too. We also have the Green Well, which will change you into a fair folk with just one sip, but for a very high price in an artist's eyes. <br><br>And right before our eyes, we get to see a beautiful story of sacrifice and love be painted. Also, this for sure has <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277792259?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>, by Sarah J. Maas, feels to it. I just seemed to be constantly reminded of ACOTAR while reading this story. Maybe it is because both stories star fae and take place for a majority in the spring court, but either way this feels like a YA ACOTAR, but Rook is way better than Tamlin.<br><br>This story held very true to fae folklore and mythology: the fair folk cannot lie, they have negative reactions to iron, they are very vain and very overly confident, they eat "interesting" food, and they wear glamour to hide what they truly look like underneath. I loved all of these aspects and the way they were seamlessly incorporated. <br><br>Isobel is an amazing female protagonist that I felt honored to read about. She was so selfless and was willing to do anything to protect her family. Also, she wouldn't let anyone or anything interfere with her passion for art and it warmed my heart completely. She was so smart, so caring, and so determined. <br><br>And Rook... Well, Rook was pretty exceptional as well. Yes, he was cocky and arrogant, but what fae court prince isn't? Rook was easy to love, too, and he also has the power to shape shift and I was completely living for any scene with Isobel interacting with him as an animal. Especially one bed time scene in particular! (I promise, this sounds way more risqué that it really is.) <br><br>The side characters in this book were simply amazing, too. Lark, Gadfly, Aster, March, May, Emma, I loved them all. I can only hope that Margaret Rogerson does not stop creating stories set in this world. There is so much potential here, and I cannot wait to see what she does next. <br><br>My only real complaint is that I just never really believed, in my heart and soul, Rook and Isobel's feelings for one another. I feel like it doesn't make sense on either of their sides, either. Like, Rook was burned once before and Isobel had a family tragedy that made her very weary of all things fae in general. Yes, she spent a few weeks painting his portrait, but they even said they didn't speak that much to one another. It was like a weird type of instalove, which never felt 100% authentic. <br><br>Yet, the true love story of this book, in my eyes, is the love between humans and being able to have an outlet to create art. I truly believe this story is a love letter to artists of all kinds, or people in general that can't imagine a life without being able to create. I loved this underlying message, and I loved how Isobel never took her gift for granted, but instead used it as a solution to a problem multiple times.<br><br>This story was a gift to read. The imagery was expertly crafted, the prose was beautiful, the characters were fantastic, and the story was absolutely addicting. This three-hundred page stand alone YA fantasy is very fast paced, immersive, and very easy to read. I read this in two sittings and once I turned the last page my only wish was for more. <br><br>Also, can Charlie Bowater do more cover art now, because this cover is nothing short of breathtaking. And it's a perfect match for the beautiful story that is inside. I completely recommend this upon release (September 26th, 2017) and I have nothing but high hopes for Margaret Rogerson and this stunning debut novel! I wish her all the success in the world and I selfishly hope she doesn't leave this fae world anytime soon.<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quote above was taken from an ARC and is subject to change upon publication.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7115047798097608863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085053036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7174257073544572529">I just read the most wonderful book! Oh, how fun it was to get my Fae on 😊<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491342268ra/22400704.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Isobel lives in Whimsy with Emma and the two adopted little girls. <br/><br/>Isobel is a most wonderful painter, this is her craft. She paints for the fae. Her most regular client over the years is Gadfly. <br/><br/>****Might be some spoilers ahead****<br/><br/>So one day, Gadfly tells Isobel she is to be visited by the autumn prince the next day to paint his portrait. Well, of course this freaks Isobel out. She rushes around trying to buy up all the p</span>
  <span id="freeText7174257073544572529" style="display:none">I just read the most wonderful book! Oh, how fun it was to get my Fae on 😊<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491342268ra/22400704.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isobel lives in Whimsy with Emma and the two adopted little girls. <br><br>Isobel is a most wonderful painter, this is her craft. She paints for the fae. Her most regular client over the years is Gadfly. <br><br>****Might be some spoilers ahead****<br><br>So one day, Gadfly tells Isobel she is to be visited by the autumn prince the next day to paint his portrait. Well, of course this freaks Isobel out. She rushes around trying to buy up all the paint she might need. On her way home she is attacked by an evilness from the fae world. BUT, the lovely autumn prince saves her. <br><br>This autumn prince is named Rook. I mean it's fitting because he can shapeshift but he mostly shifts into a raven. My heart, yes! I'm in love with him ❤️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463450440ra/19119260.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While Isobel is painting his portrait they start to enjoy each other's company but Rook is whisked away to fight in the great hunt. He sends someone for the painting and is mad at what she drew. So he decides to drag her to fae land to have a reckoning of sorts. <br><br>They get into all kinds of trouble along the way and there are some funny moments with their banter. I loved it. <br><br>Anyway, they make it to the spring court where Gadfly is and after a day, all hell breaks loose! Isobel and Rook are fighting for their lives! <br><br>But let me just say, I got my happy ending 😊💕<br><br>Happy Reading. <br><br>Mel ❤️<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/10/an-enchantment-of-ravens-by-margaret.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_2006490398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2006490398" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2006490398?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2006490398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6591210520152562651"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I wiped off my fingers, but it wasn't the mold or maggots making my stomach revolt... No, it was the knowledge that all around me sat empty people in rotting clothes, nibbling on flyblown trifles while they spoke of nothing of consequence with fixed smiles on their false faces.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Let’s just rename this book <i>An Enchantment of This User</i>, because this book’s main strength is that <b>it’s so engaging you cannot focus on the flaws.</b> This is one of those books that is just so. freaking. addicting</span>
  <span id="freeText6591210520152562651" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I wiped off my fingers, but it wasn't the mold or maggots making my stomach revolt... No, it was the knowledge that all around me sat empty people in rotting clothes, nibbling on flyblown trifles while they spoke of nothing of consequence with fixed smiles on their false faces.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Let’s just rename this book <i>An Enchantment of This User</i>, because this book’s main strength is that <b>it’s so engaging you cannot focus on the flaws.</b> This is one of those books that is just so. freaking. addicting. Were there cringey moments? Totally. Could this book have done with some editing? Yes. But would I totally recommend this? Yes. I was promised morally grey fairies, a great romance, and imagery, and this book delivered - perfectly - on all three fronts. <br /><br />Let’s break it down. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>No. You surpass us all." Beside me she looked colorless and frail. "You are like a living rose among wax flowers. We may last forever, but you bloom brighter and smell sweeter, and draw blood with your thorns.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>LET'S TALK FAIRIES.</b> Because hoooooooly shit, guys, this kind of fairy aesthetic is my freaking <i>shit</i>. Fairies in this book cannot feel - or at least, we think they cannot. So this book becomes one about <b>the virtue of emotion.</b> And not emotion from romantic love - emotion in general. One of the side characters has an arc totally revolving around her own emotional heart, without even a romantic element, and it's become one of my favorites. <br /><br />The instalove is… real. Okay, I hate when reviewers lie, so I’m not going to: Rook and Isobel have some major instalove going on, and that’s the point. But <b>to me, their actual dynamic as a couple was fantastic.</b> Honestly, guys, ever since Laini fucking Taylor, queen of instalove that gives me feelings, I have given up on my anti-instalove crusade and joined the anti-boring-couples crusade. TLDR: Isobel and Rook were an entertaining couple. <b>Instalove is fine as long as I’m not bored by the couple themselves</b>. Thanks for coming to my Ted Talk bye don’t @ me<br /><br />Okay, I’m going to make a blanket generalization and I don’t care if you liked this book or not, you have to agree with me here: <b>the writing of this book is fucking masterful.</b> The last time I got chills from a writing style alone was Anna-Marie McLemore’s <i>Wild Beauty</i>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881264915" rel="nofollow noopener">we all know how that turned out</a>. Fantastic writing can fix a ton of issues, and <i>An Enchantment of Ravens</i> has that fantastic writing down pat. <br /><br />Like, okay, I don’t want to be dragged by my lovely friends in the comments and I don’t want people to get me wrong in what I’m saying: this book had its trashy moments. A lot of them. But even the trashy moments ended up just becoming part of the fun for me because I was so freaking entertained. <b>Good couple dynamic + best writing of the year = good book.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6591210520152562651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1991509034" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991509034" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991509034?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991509034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1925221913999364953"><b>Where do I even <i>begin</i> to say how much I enjoyed this?!?</b> It's an absolutely delightful fae wild adventure, complete with a good dose of SCHEMING which I admit I am such a fan of. The ending had my Slytherin soul all up and shouting in approval. Omg this was just so good. I laughed out loud. I fell in love with the gorgeous writing. I loooooved it.<br/><br/><b>+ So it was kind of a different "fae" world to what I'm used to.</b><br/>This does the courts via all the seasons, and I still don't get why some faerie books do</span>
  <span id="freeText1925221913999364953" style="display:none"><b>Where do I even <i>begin</i> to say how much I enjoyed this?!?</b> It's an absolutely delightful fae wild adventure, complete with a good dose of SCHEMING which I admit I am such a fan of. The ending had my Slytherin soul all up and shouting in approval. Omg this was just so good. I laughed out loud. I fell in love with the gorgeous writing. I loooooved it.<br /><br /><b>+ So it was kind of a different "fae" world to what I'm used to.</b><br />This does the courts via all the seasons, and I still don't get why some faerie books do that vs some do the seelie vs unseelie courts?! Is it just an interpretation of lore or are they all completely different?? But anyway I LOVE IT. I loved the aesthetics of princes of different seasons.😍Isobel's world is caught up in an eternal summer (noiiiiice) and they end up in the Spring Courts which were (deceptively) gorgeous. <b>And this gave us faeries that can't feel human emotions.</b> They're so vapid and silly, nearly, but like deeply miserable and complex. I LOVED this version too!! <br /><br />Hopefully this will tie me over until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032887.The_Wicked_King__The_Folk_of_the_Air__2_" title="The Wicked King (The Folk of the Air #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked King</a> comes out (sobsob)<br /><br /><b>+ Isobel was the BEST narrator.</b><br />I freaking adored her. For starters she was realistic: this book features a sort of fae-roadtrip a bit, and Isobel ended up being filthy, her clothes stank, she got pimples, and she got cranky when she was hungry. LIKE HOLY HECK THIS WAS NICE TO READ. And she was addicted to art, had a knife-sharp sense of humour, and completely kept her head when like half the fae world tried to kill her. Go Isobel! (Also she was SHORT. Shout out to we short people who still get stuff done...except, ya know, reach tall cupboards.)<br /><br /><b> + And Rook was the bessst.</b><br />He was so vain lmao and like this super tall autumn prince, warrior and knight and talented magician...and yet so childlike in the face of human things. He gets so confused when Isobel needs to eat. And she totally messes with him and it's ADORABLE. I just loved how earnest and sweet he was. Like here is a prince who could be very wicked, but is actually very respectful. And I loved how vain he was, it just made my day.<br /><br /><b>+ Ok so is the romance instalove?!</b><br />It is but it's also a <i>discussion</i> about instalove. Like Isobel meets Rook to paint his portrait and she "falls in love with him". But she doesn't really. She has a fluttering crush on this otherworldly gorgeous boy...and <i>she realises this and admits it.</i> I mean obviously after they're thrown into a whirlwind journey together of monsters and the Wild Hunt and rotting castles and evil kings, and they save each other and get to know each other -- they do truly fall in love. <b>But I actually felt like this was a good example of unpacking the trope.</b><br /><br /><b>+ Also Isobel is an artists!</b><br />Faeries can't do any sort of art or creation here (I'm not sure why) so they relied on the humans for it all. Like writing or making clothes or painting etc. etc. Isobel does art and the whole book SHOWS how she's obsessed with it! <b>Like her perspective turns the book into one big gorgeous canvas.</b> The writing is so visual and dimensional, you don't just <i>read</i> faerieland, you fall facefirst into it and get entranced by the magic.<br /><br /><b>+ Other things I loooved:</b><br />☆ it actually has a scene where Isobel totally lays out that Rook is NOT to touch her without permission and like frikkin' hallelujah for books that care about respectful and unproblematic romance, especially between powerful vs unpowerful characters<br />☆ it IS SO FUNNY<br />☆ the cover is a gorgeous dream<br />☆ the ending is full of deliciously vicious twists<br />☆ i love faeries and how manipulative they are in general<br />☆ gorgeous writing<br />☆ so many ravens<br />☆ Isobel has two sisters who are enchanted into being little girls but they were goats and this is so wonderful<br />☆ i liiiiike it so much<br /><br /><br /><b>I'm so so glad I read this one.</b> It was kind of one I was worried I wouldn't like after seeing a ton of "meh" reviews but hOLD MY IRON AND SALT it was perfect for me and everything I love in a book. Whimsical and slightly vicious and entirely funny. Thank you for existing, little book.😍<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>"Yes, I know what cooking is," he said. "I was merely astonished that so many tools of your Craft can double as armaments. Is there anything you humans don't use to kill one another?"<br />"Probably not," I admitted.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Somehow I've even grown fond of your -- your irritating questions, and your short legs, and your accidental attempts to kill me."<br />I recoiled. "that's the worst declaration of love I've ever heard!"</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Yes, I can. In fact, I must. I can't let any harm befall you so it's best I stay close."<br />"You could offer to sleep on the floor, like a gentleman."<br />He appeared horrified by the suggestion.<br />"And I'm not certain you're in any state to protect me," I went on, sensing a lost cause. "Just now you were almost assassinated by a teapot."<br />"Isobel." Rook looked at me gravely. "Isobel, listen. The teapot is of no consequence. I can defeat anyone, at any time."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"You look very fine this evening, Gadfly," I said without feeling.<br />"Yes, I know," he replied. "Yet I can't deny it's wonderful to hear my suspicions confirmed."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I seized the dagger from him. Having no idea what to do with it afterward, I lifted the cushion I was lying on and shoved it underneath, then threw my weight back on top. "Stop being melodramatic! I am not going to <i>kill you</i> in my <i>parlour</i>!"<br />He stared at me in disbelief. "Did you just sit on it?"<br />"Yes," I said mutinously.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="1925221913999364953" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2158182788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2158182788" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2158182788?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=royals">royals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=donated-or-sold">donated-or-sold</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=fairies-elves">fairies-elves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2158182788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9956130531287470474"><b>This was pretty underwhelming, which is a huge bummer, because I really wanted to like it.</b><br/><br/>A lot of people might compare this at first to ACOTAR because of the fair folk and their courts, but - surprise! - fairies and their courts are actually longstanding fairy lore that go back centuries. Sarah J. Maas didn't make all that up on her own. <br/><br/>Anyway, as I said, I really wanted to like this, if only for the cover.<br/><br/>But, alas, the world building felt unfinished, the purpose and direction of the story wa</span>
  <span id="freeText9956130531287470474" style="display:none"><b>This was pretty underwhelming, which is a huge bummer, because I really wanted to like it.</b><br /><br />A lot of people might compare this at first to ACOTAR because of the fair folk and their courts, but - surprise! - fairies and their courts are actually longstanding fairy lore that go back centuries. Sarah J. Maas didn't make all that up on her own. <br /><br />Anyway, as I said, I really wanted to like this, if only for the cover.<br /><br />But, alas, the world building felt unfinished, the purpose and direction of the story was unclear to the very end, and the characters were a group of bland strangers I never truly got to know. <br /><br />I love fairy court folklore and had high hopes for this book; however, the only thing that truly impressed me here was the fact that I finished it, which again: bummer, especially since Rogerson has a very fluid and engaging writing style.<br /><br />As such, despite my lackluster response to this book, I could probably be convinced to attempt another book by her, provided the blurb sounded interesting. And I got it on sale.<br /><br />In the end, I’m glad this at least has a purty cover, since I have it in hardback via Uppercase. So at least it will look pretty on my shelves if nothing else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9956130531287470474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2120078948" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120078948" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590018789p2/10067920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120078948?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha">Samantha</a>

        rated it

<div id="review_2628766131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2628766131" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2628766131?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481497596" href="/book/show/38472041-an-enchantment-of-ravens">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2628766131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2549656949901307532">to compare this to ACOTAR is a disservice to not only the reader, but to both books, as well. it sets an impossibly high standard, one that only leads to disappointment (because we all know SJM is the queen of fae). so having seen a lot of negative reviews in regards to how this book is pitched and the comparisons made, i decided to go into this with a completely open mind and no expectations whatsoever - which i think is the only thing you can do in this particular situation. and it completely </span>
  <span id="freeText2549656949901307532" style="display:none">to compare this to ACOTAR is a disservice to not only the reader, but to both books, as well. it sets an impossibly high standard, one that only leads to disappointment (because we all know SJM is the queen of fae). so having seen a lot of negative reviews in regards to how this book is pitched and the comparisons made, i decided to go into this with a completely open mind and no expectations whatsoever - which i think is the only thing you can do in this particular situation. and it completely paid off because i quite liked this!<br /><br />the story itself is interesting. not exactly unique, but just the right amount of captivating to keep me engaged in the plot. stories about fae are pretty common, so i really enjoy how this introduces some aspects i havent previously read and provides new things to learn about that particular world. <br /><br />the writing also has a brilliant flow - so much so that i read this in nearly one sitting because i just wanted to keep reading. there is such an effortless quality to how this is written that you can go from page 1 to 100 in the blink of an eye. its just that inviting and easy to consume. <br /><br />i think people who go into this expecting it to be exactly like ACOTAR in terms of plot and quality will be a bit disappointed with this. but its a strong enough story in its own right and should be treated as such, because it definitely provided a full afternoon of light and magical entertainment for me!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2031298700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2031298700" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2031298700?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=z-2019-reads">z-2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2031298700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5446030774229655168"><b>I was gladdened by the sight of those vicious thorns more than I could say, and wondered whether the stories would have gone any differently if the princesses had been the ones telling them.</b><br/><br/>A book about star-crossed lovers, art, and a fae prince who shape shifts into a raven? YES, please!<br/><br/><b>✘ plot</b><br/>In Whimsy, humans practice Craft: cooking, artistry, writing stories, even designing clothing - all of which the fair folk are drawn to, despite their own lack of capabilities to create. Isobel is a brilli</span>
  <span id="freeText5446030774229655168" style="display:none"><b>I was gladdened by the sight of those vicious thorns more than I could say, and wondered whether the stories would have gone any differently if the princesses had been the ones telling them.</b><br /><br />A book about star-crossed lovers, art, and a fae prince who shape shifts into a raven? YES, please!<br /><br /><b>✘ plot</b><br />In Whimsy, humans practice Craft: cooking, artistry, writing stories, even designing clothing - all of which the fair folk are drawn to, despite their own lack of capabilities to create. Isobel is a brilliant portrait artist, so it's no surprise when the prince of the autumnlands, Rook, visits her for a painting. Isobel makes a fatal mistake, however, when she chooses to depict the haunting sorrow she sees in his eyes.<br /><br />As fae folk must never be shown with mortal emotions, Isobel is forced to visit the lands of the fair folk, to stand trial for her crimes against the prince. Everything shifts, though, when their relationship shifts into a beautiful love - for love between mortals and fair folk has been banned as long as time has stood, and the punishment is death.<br /><br /><b>✘ isobel</b><br />Isobel is such an enjoyable narrator, right from the very first page. Her thoughts are full of quips and snide remarks, and there's a down-to-earth sense about her that I feel like gets lost easily in the high fantasy genre. She feels wise beyond her years, yet at the same time, it's believable to think of her as a seventeen-year-old girl who's just had to grow up a little too fast.<br /><br />I was especially fond of her no-nonsense attitude and outlook on life, particularly when the story progressed and her character developed into a young woman who had to learn that not every dilemma in life can be faced with pure logic; sometimes, you have to just go with your heart.<br /><br /><b>He tried to turn away, but I touched his shoulder. Marvelously, he stilled. He was a head and a half taller than I, and the forest leapt to obey his power, but with that one touch I might as well have clapped him in irons.</b><br /><br /><b>✘ rook</b><br />Rook. ROOK. What can I even say? He's so adorable and haughty and self-obsessed and childlike and <i>fun</i>. Despite being a prince (which he reminds Isobel of often in his own self-satisfaction), he is so bewildered by human lives, and some of his assumptions and questions are so freaking cute. <br /><br />As the book progresses, there's such a tender and kindhearted aspect of his personality. His kindness is seen as a weakness among the fair folk, and it makes him a target, but he's just trying to get by in life, doing what is right and living with the fearful knowledge that everyone wants to dismantle his throne. If you like those "precious cinnamon roll" types like I do, Rook's your guy.<br /><br /><b>"Is that so terrible? You say it as though it's the most awful thing you can imagine. It isn't as though I've done it on purpose. Somehow I've even grown fond of your - your irritating questions, and your short legs, and your accidental attempts to kill me."</b><br /><br /><b>✘ side characters &amp; fair folk</b><br />- Gadfly, who is Isobel's oldest and most prominent patron. There is so much I want to say about him, but I <i>can't</i>, because it would be a huge spoiler. All I will say is that I loved Gadfly from the moment we met him, and he made me cry like the big baby I am by the time it was all said and done. What a delightfully written character.<br /><br />- March and May, Isobel's younger "sisters". They're actually <b>
  <i>goats in human form</i>
</b>, and they're freaking ADORABLE. They butt heads, and eat everything, and destroy things, and bounce around on tops of cabinets, and basically act like... well, goats. I loved them so much.<br /><br />- I also want to touch on the <b>lore</b> in this story and how it affects the fair folk. They can't touch iron, they're held to a standard of politeness that reaches compulsive levels, and they cannot lie. They pay for favors through enchantments rather than money, but are mischievous, wicked things who tend to trick the other parties into enchantments that go sour. All of these things are so prominent in the story and it showed that Margaret Rogerson actually did her homework. As someone who was obsessed with fairy lore as a kid, I'm so here for this.<br /><br /><b>✘ final thoughts</b><br />This book was a delight from start to finish, and I could barely stand to put it down for anything. I already am desperately hoping for more stories set in this world, because I could not get enough of the precious romance, or the world and magic system, or the fun characters. My <b>only</b> complaint was that it came dangerously close to insta-love, but even as someone who hates that trope, it didn't really bother me due to the way the relationship progresses.<br /><br />I loved this story so much, and I would highly recommend it to <b>anyone</b> who enjoys a good high fantasy/fae romance. This was easily one of my top reads of 2017 so far and I can't wait to see what Margaret comes up with next!<br /><br /><i>Thank you so much to Simon and Schuster for the beautiful ARC copy in exchange for my honest review. All quotes are from an unfinished copy and are subject to change.</i> <br /><br /><a href="http://howlinglibraries.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> . <a href="http://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> . <a href="http://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a> . <a href="http://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5446030774229655168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2111421939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2111421939" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2111421939?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=fantasy-read">fantasy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2111421939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10899317016248574338">First off I’d like to start by saying that this book has been compared to the <i>A Court Of Thorns And Roses</i> series a lot, which was in part why I put off reading it till now(I was afraid of disappointment), but the second I finished the first chapter I knew this was not going to be anything like the <i>A Court Of Thorns And Roses</i> series. <br/><br/>Yes, in this book there are Fair Folk and they have courts, but when have Fairies not had courts! I would be more bewildered if they didn’t have courts. And more ove</span>
  <span id="freeText10899317016248574338" style="display:none">First off I’d like to start by saying that this book has been compared to the <i>A Court Of Thorns And Roses</i> series a lot, which was in part why I put off reading it till now(I was afraid of disappointment), but the second I finished the first chapter I knew this was not going to be anything like the <i>A Court Of Thorns And Roses</i> series. <br /><br />Yes, in this book there are Fair Folk and they have courts, but when have Fairies not had courts! I would be more bewildered if they didn’t have courts. And more over, the Fairies/Fair Folk in this book have a lot more orthodox ties to the ideology of what Fairies would be before Fantasy and Young Adult literature started an evolution. The fairies are definitely more animalistic and wild than the Fae Sarah J Maas adapted and they are bound by attributes such as being incapable of lying, and being harmed by iron, which is more traditionalist but it is also a concept that has not been explored quite as much. <br /><br />The book is definitely more character driven, now I’m not saying there’s no plot, the plot is there but as you read it’s mostly about how the characters come to realize that they’re falling in love, and that’s how half the plot comes into play. The first half of the storyline is that Isobel paints mortal sorrow in the eyes of the Autumn Prince’s Portrait which causes uproar in the Autumn Court because to the Fair Folk emotions are weakness and feelings are a crime. The second half is that Isobel and the Autumn Prince fall in love, which violates the Good Law that states no mortal and Fairy can fall in love, if they do it’s an offence punishable by death and so the plot unravels before our eyes.<br /><br />Isobel is a great protagonist and I loved watching her handle herself so wonderfully in the Fairy Courts. Isobel is a painter, the greatest if her generation which makes her the most coveted artist to the Fair Folk. She lived in a town called Whimsy which is full of people willing to sell their Craft to the Fair Folk. The reason Craft is so coveted among the Fair Folk is that they can’t perform any Craft of their own, if they even try to do the smallest of Crafts they will die within a few instants. Doing business with the Fair Folk is a very perilous task, for the Fair Folk will twist your words in an instant if they are given the chance. A deal worded wrongly might even lead to the destruction of your life. <br /><br />In my opinion, I think Isobel was very clever at times where many people would not know what to do. She has been doing business with the Fairies ever since she could hold a brush in her hands, and has perfected her dealings with them. Watching her survive this arduous journey proved to be very engrossing.<br />As deadly as they are, I must say watching the Fair Folk interact with humans is ridiculous. The Fairies are so blind to the ways of the human species that they don’t even understand the basest of our needs, and therefore watching the Autumn Prince be constantly confused or amused by our protagonist gets hilarious. <br /><br />I loved this book and the Fair Folk it presented. It was a delightful read and I recommend to anyone who likes the concept of Fairies and new outlooks on Fair Folk. Like I said in the beginning of this review, many people have compared it to the <i>A Court Of Thorns And Roses</i> series, but I think no one can truly know if you will like this book till you read it. I had a great time with this book and these Fairies Margaret Rogerson created, I rate this book 4 stars.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"And we wouldn't live happily ever after, because I don't believe in such nonsense, but we both had a long, bold adventure ahead of us, and a great deal to look forward to at last." </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10899317016248574338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
