<div id="review_2014539865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2014539865" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2014539865?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2014539865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10439033251245592330"><b>“Where are half-stars when you need them?” </b><br/><br/>- Katerina, A Frustrated Goodreader<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens' title='An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson' rel='nofollow noopener'>An Enchantment of Ravens</a> is a great example of why half-stars are essential. It does not deserve 3 stars. It was ideal to make my mind drift and explore uncharted territories, to forget all those tiny and huge daily things that make me lose my sleep. <i>Why not give it 4 stars then, Kat? </i> one could wonder. Well, because I feel that those past months I've matured as a reader - and reviewer - and I came to accept that 3 sta</span>
  <span id="freeText10439033251245592330" style="display:none"><b>“Where are half-stars when you need them?” </b><br><br>- Katerina, A Frustrated Goodreader<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens" title="An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens</a> is a great example of why half-stars are essential. It does not deserve 3 stars. It was ideal to make my mind drift and explore uncharted territories, to forget all those tiny and huge daily things that make me lose my sleep. <i>Why not give it 4 stars then, Kat? </i> one could wonder. Well, because I feel that those past months I've matured as a reader - and reviewer - and I came to accept that 3 stars is not a bad rating, and that 4 (and especially 5) stars should be saved for the books I truly enjoy. 3 stars means that <b>it was a pleasant reading experience, but it did not sweep me off my feet</b>. Even though I wanted to so badly.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508351330ra/24205293.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens" title="An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15455603.Margaret_Rogerson" title="Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">Margaret Rogerson</a> painted in earthy pigments, inspired by the rusty autumn leaves, the story of a young artist, Isobel, and her encounter with a Fae Prince, Rook, the tornado that brought change to her otherwise stale life. They embarked on a journey that led them to dreadful beasts and cunning fae who hid their ugliness beneath fancy glamours and lavish clothes, they faced and fought their own nature, and battled against their demons, only to emerge stronger, and to experience a love powerful enough to destroy them. <br><blockquote>
  <b>“Why do we desire, above all other things, that which has the greatest power to destroy us?” </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Isobel and Rook's story was marvelous, on its own.</b> It featured a likable heroine who craved adventure, or simply something different from the endless summer and predictable routine that comprised her life, and a hero whose world was full of politics and intrigue, and love was considered a weakness. They passed various stages, from anger to mistrust to shy friendship before their feelings drowned them, and their interactions were both delightful and heated. What bothered me, though, was <b>the feeble world-building</b>. What other edicts did the Good Law pass? What the World Beyond was like? Why was Whimsy so special? What about the Winter Court and the Wild Hunt? Why did all Crafts physically affect the Fae so much? All of those subjects were scarcely and superficially touched, and they were mentioned as if their content was already known, I was constantly restless because something was missing. And the world-building was not the only thing missing.<br><br><b>There was magic. </b> I could feel it in the air, on the tips of my fingers and my tongue, it caressed my skin but <b>it did not consume me</b>. The writing was whimsical, there was rare beauty in it, but it escaped my grasp. I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens" title="An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens</a> a week ago, but as hard as I may try to recall the feelings it provoked, and the impression it left me, I come up empty. And it saddens me to no end, because this novel was full of potential, ready to burst and burn burn burn, but it never did.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393420015ra/8709249.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Some leniency is required, though, because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30969741.An_Enchantment_of_Ravens" title="An Enchantment of Ravens by Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">An Enchantment of Ravens</a> is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15455603.Margaret_Rogerson" title="Margaret Rogerson" rel="nofollow noopener">Margaret Rogerson</a>'s debut, and despite its flaws she proved that she can write, and I have to <b>commend her for her creativity and imagination</b>. I am positive her future works will reflect the magniture of her talent!<br><br><b>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/876-anenchantmentofravens" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on <a href="http://booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a>!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10439033251245592330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8382018039159354774" style="display:none"><u>It's official:</u> <br><br>I am on <b>Team Really Enjoyed It!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551148895ra/27119020.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isobel, a human girl, is a highly skilled and renowned portraitist. A raw, uncensored 'human' emotion. <br><br>More specifically, sorrow. She paints his portrait, displaying that feeling in his eyes.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551212751ra/27122193.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Upon seeing the portrait, Rook unexpectedly flies into a rage. How dare she paint him as such? <br><br>Before Isobel realizes what is happening, he goes all Lord Grantham on her...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551212751ra/27122196.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...and snatches her away to travel to the Autumnlands to stand trial for her insolence. However as their journey begins, they notice that something seems to be amiss in the world of the Fae. <br><br>Soon they find themselves being hunted and even worse, falling for one another.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505124805ra/23886511.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a beautifully written story of forbidden love. I was left wanting more! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510948820ra/24471131.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would recommend this to anyone who enjoys a little whimsy in their love stories. <br><br>I am really looking forward to Rogerson's next book, <i>Sorcery of Thorns</i>. If it is anything like this one, I know I will be swooning for it!</span>

<div id="review_3448434105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3448434105" />
    <a title="Vibur" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77981976-vibur"><img alt="Vibur" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542451413p2/77981976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3448434105?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vibur" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vibur" href="/user/show/77981976-vibur">Vibur</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3448434105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2849971768479872874">WHAT. THE. SHIT. WAS. THIS.<br/>(<i>rant. alert.</i>)<br/><br/>The writing is in that weird territory between beautiful and, well... <i>rubbish</i>. I mean, points for creativity and all, but this was <b>page <i>after </i>page of overly descriptive <i>tripe</i>.</b><br/>"<i>Butit'ssobeau-ti-ful!</i>"—again, the voice inside me that loves spouting off potential arguments. Oh, the writing is "beautiful" alright, for being stuffed full of useless, trifling fluff about <i>nothing</i>. See, the problem isn't the stupidly indulgent detail itself—it's that <b>there's no po</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2849971768479872874" style="display:none">WHAT. THE. SHIT. WAS. THIS.<br />(<i>rant. alert.</i>)<br /><br />The writing is in that weird territory between beautiful and, well... <i>rubbish</i>. I mean, points for creativity and all, but this was <b>page <i>after </i>page of overly descriptive <i>tripe</i>.</b><br />"<i>Butit'ssobeau-ti-ful!</i>"—again, the voice inside me that loves spouting off potential arguments. Oh, the writing is "beautiful" alright, for being stuffed full of useless, trifling fluff about <i>nothing</i>. See, the problem isn't the stupidly indulgent detail itself—it's that <b>there's no point to said stupidly indulgent detail. </b><br />The thing is, the writing is showy to the nth <i>goddarn</i> degree. And I admit, I'd have loved it, if there'd been more to it than the author embellishing the <i>entire</i> shit out of the settings—if there'd been more to it than <b>stupidly and gaudily dressed-up descriptions of <i>trees</i>, ugh.</b><br /><br />The characterisations are nonsensically <i>in-con-sist-tent</i> (I'm angry, alright?). <b>The characters flip-flop all over the place like half-cooked pancakes</b>, and, <i>wooow</i>, I'd have never guessed this was the same person from, uh, <i>ten</i> paragraphs ago. I'm sorry, but what pile of wishy-washy shit is this person's, um, "personality" meant to be, again? <br /><b>And the plot's a <i>goddarn</i> literal dumpster fire.</b> There I was, inhaling the poisonous plumes of its stupor as I gasped for air, the life suffocating out of me, insides all smouldering to dust... until, I was, at last, <i>nomore.</i> <br /><br />Alright, the point is, the plot's poorly, <i>poorly</i> put together. Nothing happens in the first half, apart from some road-tripping in the middle of… someplace (well, don't blame me, <b>the worldbuilding's nothing but absent</b>). Now, I pushed through, hoping against hope the plot would pull its <i>shit</i> together.<br />(It didn't. If possible, it got, well, <i>shittier</i>, and the flies, too, would be as repulsed as I was at this point.)<br /><b>No lie, I've <i>never</i> read a more (less?) eighth-assed ending than this</b>—<br />(Was there a "conflict"? Well, I didn't notice a <i>goddarn</i> thing.)<br />—aaand guess what? This reader doesn't want to write more of this review than this novel deserves, and will now retire to sleep to replenish her ailing, tired spirit. <br /><br />1.0/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="2849971768479872874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2848795985" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2848795985" />
    <a title="Cardan Greenbriar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93341192-cardan-greenbriar"><img alt="Cardan Greenbriar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573666059p2/93341192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2848795985?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cardan Greenbriar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cardan Greenbriar" href="/user/show/93341192-cardan-greenbriar">Cardan Greenbriar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93341192-cardan-greenbriar?shelf=it-was-good">it-was-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2848795985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9297636443638750780"><u>*i decided to increase my rating in the re-read cuz i guess while re-reading i got the self-taught hacks and cheats on where to skim and where to read slowly and absorb every word<br/> <br/><br/><br/>oh who the fuck am i kidding Rook is just <b>that hot</b><br/><br/>i mean look at him: <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576850328i/28642091._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='320' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>ok sorry,<i> this </i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576850328i/28642092._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='470' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/morgana0anagrom/?hl=en' rel='nofollow noopener'>perfectartby</a><br/><br/><br/>just remember: to enjoy this (if you don't like an ocean of forest description, skim the part which looks like a huge brick, trust me it'll 'enhance' reading experience*</u><br/><br/>Original review:<br/><br/><p>
  <i>
    <b>"No human had ever visited a</b></i></p></span>
  <span id="freeText9297636443638750780" style="display:none"><u>*i decided to increase my rating in the re-read cuz i guess while re-reading i got the self-taught hacks and cheats on where to skim and where to read slowly and absorb every word<br> <br><br><br>oh who the fuck am i kidding Rook is just <b>that hot</b><br><br>i mean look at him: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576850328i/28642091._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>ok sorry,<i> this </i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576850328i/28642092._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="470" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/morgana0anagrom/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">perfectartby</a><br><br><br>just remember: to enjoy this (if you don't like an ocean of forest description, skim the part which looks like a huge brick, trust me it'll 'enhance' reading experience*</u><br><br>Original review:<br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"No human had ever visited a fairy court and lived. Or at least, none had ever done so and remained human. I was a master of the Craft, escorted by a prince, but I had to wonder whether I truly was a special case, or if every mortal deluded themselves into thinking they were an exception to the rule."</b>
  </i>
</p><br><br><i>
  <b>DANG</b>
</i><br><br>After reading Sorcery Of Thorns I fell in love with that book, so somehow I ended up with this and I was sooooo excited. *takes shaky breath* entering this book was like rushing off to a colorful balloon in a distance only to find out that the balloon was half-deflated.<br><br>what happened with me<br>I sat down, on a sofa , with this book, I started it and after 40 pages... I.GOT.DIZZY!<br><br><s>The Story</s> Expansion of book synopsis<br>Isobel-is-a-child-prodigy-painter-who-lives-with-her-aunt-Emma-and-twin-sisters-March-and-May-paints-fair-ones-(aka faerie)-in-exchange-for-enchantments-to-her-house-such-as-chicken-eggs-and-spells-to-protect-her-house-this-and-that-prince-rook-comes-{MEGA ATTRACTION THE ONES WE SEE IN NON FANTASY NOVELS}-Isobel-ends-up-painting-his-eyes-wrong-read-back-of-the-synopsis-Isobel-and-Rook-go-on-for-HALF-OF-A-BOOK-TRAVEL-10/22 CHAPTERS YOU GUYS 10 OUT OF 22 CHAPTERS!!!! FILLED WITH DETAILS OF MOSSES, TWIGS, BIRD SOUNDS, STONES, SWEAT, AND IN THE LEAST AMOUNT ... INTIMATE WONDERS AND ATTRACTION (which obviously needed to be more)<br><i>That's where the writing went wrong. </i><br><br>The fair ones of these courts were so weird. mostly they behaved like well-mannered zombies, which was kind of terrifying, they did not know how to use any sort of craft AT ALL. i guess it was a threat to them as well, but their behavior and hidden hatred towards mortals was actually jealousy. <br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"I wiped off my fingers, but it wasn't the mold or maggots making my stomach revolt... No, it was the knowledge that all around me sat empty people in rotting clothes, nibbling on flyblown trifles while they spoke of nothing of consequence with fixed smiles on their false faces."<br></b>
  </i>
</p><br><br><br>But come <i>onnn</i>. I felt like reading Peeta and Katniss during their 'walks' in the Hunger Games. <br>And then there were unnecessary details.<br><br>here is ONE very long paragraph (my apologies):<br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"Dim as it was, the forest glowed. The golden leaves flashing by blazed like sparks caught in the updraft of a fire. A scarlet carpet unrolled before us, rich and flawless as velvet. Rising from the forest floor, the black, tangled roots breathed a bluish mist that reduced the farthest trees’ trunks to ghostly silhouettes, yet left their foliage’s luminous hues untouched. Vivid moss speckled the branches like tarnished copper. The crisp spice of pine sap infused the cool air over a musty perfume of dry leaves. A knot swelled in my throat. I couldn’t look away. There was too much of it, too fast. I’d never be able to drink it all in—I needed to absorb every leaf, every chip of bark, every flake of moss. I clenched my fingers in Rook’s mane, ravenous for my paintbrush, my easel. Sitting up straighter, I let the wind rush over me and fill my lungs to bursting. It still wasn’t enough. After seventeen years of living in a world that never changed, I felt as though I’d just flung off a stifling wool sweater and felt the breeze on my skin for the very first time. Nothing would ever be enough again."<br><br></b>
  </i>
</p><br><br><br><b>*sighs* </b><br>and every page had a paragraph like this. Look i get it that she is a child prodigy and an artist. I get it how painters describe EVERY SINGLE DETAIL, but some don't, and even if 'detailed' description of something was needed then make it Rook's handsomeness or his behavior towards Isobel. not-the-forest-please-for-the-love-of-sanity.<br><br><br><u>
  <b>The characters:</b>
</u><br><b>Isobel:</b> A 17 year old prodigy, who describes everything ... in a forest. period.<br><br><b>Rook: </b>The autumn prince. Caring. Passionate. and has tendency to get hopeless and sulk.<br><br><b> Gadfly: </b> Thank goodness for his presence in this book, he entertained me so much. Gadfly plays a very important role in this book. He's Isobel's client for a while. As being spring prince he does have quite power but Gadfly has his own intentions to bring Isobel to Autumn-lands and Spring-lands. and of course he plays the perfect gentleman all decent and restrained.<br><br><b>Lark: </b> Gadfly's niece. Living in spring court. Lark reminded me of 2 things. One, the rhyme on baby t.v. that was my favorite when I was a child.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560576363ra/27671168.gif" width="340" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>she behaves like this as well</i><br><br>Two, of that curious energetic 10 year old girl that hosts you when you go to somebody's house and she accidentally <b>ends up giving you food poisoning or breaks your leg.</b><br>Like Gadfly, she also kept me amused. of-course. <br><br><br><b>
  <u>The writing</u>
</b><br>'_'<br>ohhhh dear lord, i wish painting books contained this much details rather than fantasy novels. <br>and also some of the quotes from this book made me cringe<br>here's one:<br><br><b>ummm errr</b><br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"A storm gathered in my breast; the butterflies fell fluttering weakly to the ground.<br><br>With a sharp intake of breath, Rook looked away."<br></b>
  </i>
</p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502047908ra/23521052.gif" width="270" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br><br><b>continuing with story</b><br>somewhere around the end of their travel, Gadfly (prince of spring court) takes them to his land, they spend some days there but here is the thing: there is a law, it's called the Good Law<br><br> <b>Dictionary</b><br>Good Law (law): that a fair one and a mortal should not fall in love together. <br>Green well: a source of water river/well/spring with that type of water that when someone drinks from it they 'die' and become immortal<br><br>during their travel Rook and Isobel fall in love with each other. this becomes a problem because they are breaking the good law. A ONE hella problem.<br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"Love between us was impossible. I forced myself to confront what would become of us if I allowed this feeling to take flight. There were only two options: drink from the Green Well, or condemn us both to death. "</b>
  </i>
</p><br><br>I liked the story, really did, about how Rook was attracted to Isobel from the beginning and vice versa, how he takes care of her 'mortal necessities' and learns them, how he protects her, stands up for her. Rook's and Isobel's relationship i just loved it! I adored Rook from the beginning, he was so gentle and caring towards Isobel. Even the way he looked at her showed so much affection.<br><br><br><p>
  <i>
    <b>"He really is in love with me,I thought. My heart leapt forward like a startled deer. Seeing a confession of love in his eyes was nothing like hearing it declared aloud. This was a look that would make time stop, if it could. Soft and sharp at once, an aching tenderness edged with sorrow, naked proof of a heart already broken. Here I stood in a dragonfly dress, holding his arm, and he knew our time was almost over."</b>
  </i>
</p><br><br><br>I really wanted this book to become my favorite, bummer it didn't. I had absolute no negative thoughts about this book before reading but i will say that the author's writing has improved so much, the next stand alone by Margaret is MAGNIFICENT! do give it a try <br><br><b>Have a happy day in the forest!<br>and paint trees and be happy!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560575889i/27671151._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9297636443638750780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2150241918" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2150241918" />
    <a title="Swaye " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10675488-swaye"><img alt="Swaye " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528889426p2/10675488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2150241918?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Swaye " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Swaye " href="/user/show/10675488-swaye">Swaye </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781481497602" href="/book/show/35011486-an-enchantment-of-ravens">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10675488-swaye?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10675488-swaye?shelf=books">books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150241918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2047934533420209281"><b>WTF DID I JUST READ.</b><br/><br/>This book is like Hotel California. You can check out any time you like (and you will, mentally, many, many times - trust me!), but you can never leave! <br/><br/>After the Twilight series I never dreamed another <s>really goddamn awful</s> book would come along that would have the strange, voodeedoo power of compelling me to read to the very last page, despite every ounce of good sense begging me to kick it to the curb. And yes, I know a pretty cover is not a good reason to read a book, I sh</span>
  <span id="freeText2047934533420209281" style="display:none"><b>WTF DID I JUST READ.</b><br><br>This book is like Hotel California. You can check out any time you like (and you will, mentally, many, many times - trust me!), but you can never leave! <br><br>After the Twilight series I never dreamed another <s>really goddamn awful</s> book would come along that would have the strange, voodeedoo power of compelling me to read to the very last page, despite every ounce of good sense begging me to kick it to the curb. And yes, I know a pretty cover is not a good reason to read a book, I should have known better, I only have myself to blame, yada yada, but I'm claiming ensorcellment and sticking with it! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508513261i/24221987.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Now, normally a 300 page book would take me about 2 or 3 days at the most, but this was an arduous 5 day slog. The "what the fucks" come at you pretty thick and fast, and when it seems <i>absolutely</i> impossible to get any worse or more bizarre, it does, and with serious melodramatic gusto! Here is actual footage of me reading this book: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502953595ra/23613186.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, with that happening every few pages, sometimes every few lines, a mere 5 days is rather a miraculous feat in and of itself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508513261ra/24221988.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's not that the pacing is slow, in fact its just the opposite. Everything happens too quickly and nothing feels well thought out or believable. As many bewildered readers before me have mentioned, there are heaping helpings of the dreaded insta-love, which is ALMOST forgivable in the very beginning because our protagonist (who we never find out the real name of, lets call her Margaret) actually knows its ridiculous and never fails to mention its ridiculosity every time the big L-word comes up. Buuuuut, she goes hurtling headlong into it regardless!<br><br>Then, not to get too spoilery, but I couldn't quite wrap my head around what she was kissing when his glamour fell away? His fangs? His decaying lips? I'm all for "it's what's on the inside that counts" but COME ON, Margaret, that's pushing it! <br><br>By the time I got to it I wasn't surprised that the ending was a mashed together, all-too convenient happily ever after, in which there are so many loose ends it is a wonder that this book is a standalone. (A fact for which I, personally, am extremely grateful. I'd rather pretend this never happened.)<br><br>In many, <i>many</i> reviews of this book I have read variations on the phrase, "But I have questions!" And to those sweet, summer children I say: There are no answers, dear ones! Our new friend Margaret was either recounting a fever dream or tripping <i>
  <b>serious</b>
</i> balls while writing this. We can only hope that she is okay now and move on with our lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2047934533420209281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1992882072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1992882072" />
    <a title="Viktoria Winter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36437228-viktoria-winter"><img alt="Viktoria Winter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528870929p2/36437228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1992882072?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Viktoria Winter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Viktoria Winter" href="/user/show/36437228-viktoria-winter">Viktoria Winter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=inspiring-characters">inspiring-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=favorite-moments">favorite-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=amazing-character-development">amazing-character-development</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36437228-viktoria-winter?shelf=recieved-for-review">recieved-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992882072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8178527993922163866"><b>Disclaimer: This book is a spring banquet of ripe grapefruit wine, a summer morning beneath swaying willow trees, an autumnal bonfire deep in the woods, and a wintry dusk backset to the wind. </b><br/><br/>….At least it made me feel that way. Rogerson <i>killed</i> the imagery game. It was glorious. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497295436ra/23009210.gif' width='350' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I’ve been waiting for a very long time for a book like this to come out. I’ve always been obsessed with faeries and elvish folklore, and while I’ve read just about every book related to those mythologies nothing ever se</span>
  <span id="freeText8178527993922163866" style="display:none"><b>Disclaimer: This book is a spring banquet of ripe grapefruit wine, a summer morning beneath swaying willow trees, an autumnal bonfire deep in the woods, and a wintry dusk backset to the wind. </b><br><br>….At least it made me feel that way. Rogerson <i>killed</i> the imagery game. It was glorious. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497295436ra/23009210.gif" width="350" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I’ve been waiting for a very long time for a book like this to come out. I’ve always been obsessed with faeries and elvish folklore, and while I’ve read just about every book related to those mythologies nothing ever seemed quite right. Sure, all of the characters had pointy ears, magical powers, and lived somewhat near the forest, but that’s about where the similarities cut off. I wanted a story where the Fae were humanoid with tree roots for limbs and flowers for lips, where they worshipped nature instead of just lived in it— something closer to the rendition of Celtic folklore including the Wild Hunt, changelings, and caverns beneath the earth. And I’m so happy to say that An Enchantment of Ravens was that book for me. <br><br>Our narrator is a young portrait artist named Isobel who lives in a village called Whimsy where it is eternally summer. Her Craft— a form of human creativity that cannot be done by Fair Folk without risk of harm—is legendary for someone her age, and various Fair Ones come to visit her parlor to be painted, if only for a small price. All masters of Craft receive enchantments as a form of payment, but if worded wrong these wishes can go awry. Isobel always wishes for practical things and words them right, much to the delight of her regular client and wish-granter Gadfly. But upon one of his usual visits, Gadfly tells Isobel that she should expect the Autumn Prince soon. And while she gets to know Rook more intimately than any of her other clients, she accidentally paints mortal sorrow into his eyes. For this, the price is grave, and now Rook must take Isobel to his home, the Autumnlands, to stand trial for what she has done. However, they might never make it there with what lurks between her world and his kingdom. <br><br>The writing, the plot, the characters, the romance….everything in this book is a treat. At first I thought that it might be a bit fast-paced because it’s just a tad smaller in length to some of my more recent reads, but that’s definitely not the case. It was well thought out from the start to the finish with no “filler” scenes or rushed pivotal moments. I took my time reading this book and it really helped me delve into the setting so much so that I felt a deep connection with the main characters by the commencement of the final page. <br><br>As I’ve mentioned before, one of the deal-breaking moments for me was the rendition of the Fae. The Fair Folk in this book cannot lie, are harmed by iron, have humanoid skins they wear as a disguise to hide their more monstrous forms underneath, live in places made of all things natural, and (my favorite) don’t have emotions. Supposedly. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500054814ra/23294811.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One thing that always stood out to me amongst these other faerie novels was that the authors were quick to include emotion of some sort amongst their kind, wherein the original tales depicted the Fae as cruel, often vindictive and evil characters that didn't feel human emotion and rather loved to toil with it for their own reprieve. That being said, the only romance featured in this book is saved for the main characters—which I thought was a wonderful decision as opposed to the usual minor “ships” that are often sidelined and then forced to fulfill plot devices. Also, it made the story seem more like a fairytale which was entirely the vibe I got from it (a morbid, eerily beautiful fairytale at that). <br><br> <i>“He was no more able to understand the sorrow of a human’s death than a fox might mourn the killing of a mouse.”</i><br><br>Not to be dramatic, but I think I’ve found my favorite YA male protagonist as well. I had gone into this book believing that the Autumn Prince would be brooding with a side of dark humor (you know the type, I’m sure) but you can imagine my utter surprise when I find that Rook is, in fact, quite the opposite. He is good-natured, apologizes whenever he thinks he’s upset someone even when he hasn’t, doesn’t understand human emotion and finds it terrifying, and has a deep love for autumn. There were many hysterical moments between Rook and Isobel but I won’t mention them here because they’re something you should experience on your own. However, I will say that when someone bows or curtsies to a Fair One, that Fae must return the gesture immediately.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500054461ra/23294731.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>His character development is prominent throughout the story, as is Isobel’s, but I won’t mention more for fear of spoiling you. Rest assured, there were many things I picked up on that had changed from the beginning to the end, and they changed for the better. I also adore the way in which his physical descriptor was written:<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <i>"…against his golden-brown complexion, which put me in mind of late-afternoon sunlight dappling fallen leaves.” </i>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And I think it’s important to note that he has ADHD, something my brother suffers from, and I found it refreshing to see this trait with a main character for a change. Did I mention that he can also transform into a dark horse and a raven? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500054461ra/23294732.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’ve already re-read this story three times and each time brings about stronger emotions for me. This is one of those books that you’ll want to revisit frequently because it plays with your heart in ways no other stories have (at least that’s the case for me)! The ending was wild, and while everything was answered and little to no ties were left untangled, I still want more. As of now I believe this is a stand-alone, but if there were ever a sequel in it’s future there would be plenty of things to write further more from where this book ended. If not that, then you can expect I’ll be dabbling in my fair share of Fanfiction. Enough said: READ THIS BOOK.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8178527993922163866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2403863736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2403863736" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2403863736?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=faeries-elves">faeries-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2403863736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17598296624281393900">This was a buddy read with my sister-from-another-mister, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420642988' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laura</a>! <3 We’re so great at these that we spent the majority of the discussions speaking about literally everything <i>except</i> this book, haha. Go, us! :P<br/><br/>This might be a <b>semi-rant</b>, so fair warning!<br/><br/>OK! So, in case you didn’t know, faeries are some of my favourite supernatural creatures, hence my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825-the-cruel-prince' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> (aka the <b>Queen of the Fae</b>, as is acknowledged by the YA book community) obsession. <br/><br/>Going into this, I heard “OMG, this is just like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_' title='A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Cour</a></span>
  <span id="freeText17598296624281393900" style="display:none">This was a buddy read with my sister-from-another-mister, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420642988" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a>! &lt;3 We’re so great at these that we spent the majority of the discussions speaking about literally everything <i>except</i> this book, haha. Go, us! :P<br /><br />This might be a <b>semi-rant</b>, so fair warning!<br /><br />OK! So, in case you didn’t know, faeries are some of my favourite supernatural creatures, hence my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032825-the-cruel-prince" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> (aka the <b>Queen of the Fae</b>, as is acknowledged by the YA book community) obsession. <br /><br />Going into this, I heard “OMG, this is just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>” over and over again! And I can attest that…yes, this is…because I didn’t like ACOTAR either!!! UGHHHH!!! There were even quotes, which I swear sounded just like something Sarah J. Maas would write…e.g. <i>“It was unmistakably him…”</i> (Don’t tell me that Maas never wrote lines like this). I was half-expecting the word “male” to be thrown about left, right, and centre.<br /><br />Having said that, there was <b>one quote</b> that I really enjoyed, which was: <i>“Why do we desire, above all other things, that which has the greatest power to destroy us?”</i> If only the rest of the book contained profound quotes like that! It would’ve been infinitely better!!!<br /><br />While Margaret Rogerson is definitely a capable writer, her descriptions were <i>too flowery</i>, while the overall plot and characters were simultaneously <i>written too simply</i>, causing this book to feel awfully <b>disjointed</b>. In addition, at the beginning of the novel, the point of view switches from first person to second person quite frequently, which leads me to believe that this novel could definitely have benefitted from <b>another round of editing</b>. <br /><br />Moving on to the plot…there wasn’t really any??? It definitely resembled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/822613.The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_" title="The Fellowship of the Ring (The Lord of the Rings, #1) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fellowship of the Ring</a>, in the sense that a great deal of the novel is spent <b>travelling</b> from one faerie land to another (springlands, autumnlands, winterlands, summerlands). There doesn’t seem to be any goal or final destination. The characters just appear to be moving aimlessly along, while the reader sits wondering as to the point of all this. The synopsis leads the reader to believe that there shall be an epic fight against the Alder King…HAHAHA no. Talk about <b>anticlimactic</b>. <br /><br />As for the characters, aside from <b>Rook</b> (a faerie) and <b>March &amp; May</b> (an adorable goat-to-human set of twins), I couldn’t really care less about any of the characters, especially Isobel. <b>Isobel</b> has to be the most <i>arrogant, egotistical, condescending, idiotic, helpless, and insipid</i> protagonist that I’ve come across in a while. And let’s not forget this gem: <i>“He was arrogant, self-centred, and obtuse—unworthy of me in every way.”</i> Why anyone would fall in love with her is beyond me! <br /><br />Also, I’d like to mention that <b>instalove</b> begins right off the bat here. By Chapter <i>Four</i>, Isobel is already in love with Rook. And despite dragging her off to await trial in the autumnlands (not a spoiler; it’s in the synopsis, so don’t freak out), he somehow has fallen in love with her, even though he spent the majority of the time fighting faerie beasts and protecting her, whilst she <i>stood there and did nothing</i> (well, she panicked, but not much else)!<br /><br />I had really hoped that this would be my new favourite faery novel, as the only faery novels that I’ve loved thus far are written by either Holly Black or Cassandra Clare. However, it seems that this book was not as enjoyable as I thought it would be, unfortunately. This book was definitely well-written and it had the <b>potential</b> to be great, but regrettably, that potential was ultimately wasted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17598296624281393900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17109101504938552141"><b>2 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“You are like a living rose among wax flowers. We maybe last forever, but you bloom brighter and smell sweeter....”</blockquote>
</i><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507666398i/24137525.png' width='280' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If you listen very carefully, legend says you can still hear my drawn-out sigh, drifting in the wind…All these mystical, magical things were supposed to be <i>enchanting</i> but I just felt <i>meh.</i> <br/><br/>And it starts off really good! <b>This has a gorgeous setting with a captivating depiction of fae.</b> Rogerson's clever use of description builds picturesque scenes and there are <i>so</i> many fun e</span>
  <span id="freeText17109101504938552141" style="display:none"><b>2 Stars</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“You are like a living rose among wax flowers. We maybe last forever, but you bloom brighter and smell sweeter....”</blockquote>
</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507666398i/24137525.png" width="280" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you listen very carefully, legend says you can still hear my drawn-out sigh, drifting in the wind…All these mystical, magical things were supposed to be <i>enchanting</i> but I just felt <i>meh.</i> <br><br>And it starts off really good! <b>This has a gorgeous setting with a captivating depiction of fae.</b> Rogerson's clever use of description builds picturesque scenes and there are <i>so</i> many fun elements introduced in the first few chapters, including: <br><br>- Twin-goats turned into mischievous children<br>- Pompous fae obsessed with self-image, but more than a little out of touch.<br>-<b> Creepy half fae and half-dead human zombie spirit deer thing</b><br>- Fae who literally <i>die</i> if they create anything (‘craft’)<br>- As such, a whole town who creates for the fae in exchange for magical favors <br>- Fae who often twist the favors into not-so pleasant loopholes <b>(see goat-children)</b><br>- The town is <i>literally</i> named Whimsy<br><br>BUT, it took less than three chapters for this to turn into <b>another story where the sensible heroine goes ga-ga after instalove.</b> Isobel is a master of craft and cleverly receives practical favors from the fae in return. She’s firmly established as <i>smart</i> and <i>careful</i> doing whatever she can to keep her family safe. ...And then Rook walks in. And <i>I just don’t understand?</i> She was sure she loved him… because why? She’s sees sadness in his eyes, and she wasn’t aware fae were capable of human emotion? <b>Just because he’s hot and <i>able</i> to love doesn’t mean you love him, girl!</b> There seriously wasn't a full conversation before she was dropping the L-bomb. <br><br>Don’t get me wrong-- conversation does happen! <b> Over a meandering, long journey that exists simply to force interaction between the love interests.</b> Seriously. Rook decides Isobel must stand trial for her heinous actions (<i>She painted him with sadness in his eyes, guys!</i>) and they take off towards Fairy-Land. But then they change directions five-times, more zombie-deer show up, they end up at a spring party and just… a bunch of other random crap? <b>There wasn’t really any plot outside of, “these guys are totally going to fall in love, and they aren’t supposed to.”</b><br><br>However, there were several things I liked about the ending. There is some devious fae twisting-and-turning, and Isobel’s intelligence comes back as she proves she <i>is</i> capable. But by then it was too late, I’d already forgotten to care about the characters. <br><br><b>And there's no good resolution for anything?</b> Everything is either<br> 1.) solved way too easily,<br>- like the incredibly evil and built up Alder-King<br>- ALL his oppressive laws. <br><br>2.) it's not really solved at all? <br>- Like the fact that Isobel is going to age and die while Rook stays the same forever? <br><br><b>Overall:</b><br>Lots of pretty people and pretty words, not enough substance. There isn’t really a plot outside of the forbidden instalove, so if that’s your thing, you’re in luck. <br><br>I received an ARC of this in exchange for an honest review, thanks to <i>Simon and Schuster</i> for the opportunity!<br><br>(Also, all this talk of ‘crafting’ am I the only one that remembers:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507665758i/24137487._SY540_.jpg" width="362" height="362" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> )</span>

<div id="review_2202169931" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202169931" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2202169931?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=wheres-your-editor">wheres-your-editor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=sent-from-pub">sent-from-pub</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202169931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15813705542919587680">Thanks Simon & Schuster for the free review copy!<br/><br/>I'm so appalled at this book because it's so long since I've read a book and thought, "How did this get published?? It still needs so much work." This genuinely feels like the first draft of a book, there are SO many technical issues that don't make sense.<br/><br/>This book is trying to be acomaf… except with the worst parts of Twilight sprinkled into it. First of all, there is such a power imbalance between fae & humans that is emphasized and often exploi</span>
  <span id="freeText15813705542919587680" style="display:none">Thanks Simon &amp; Schuster for the free review copy!<br /><br />I'm so appalled at this book because it's so long since I've read a book and thought, "How did this get published?? It still needs so much work." This genuinely feels like the first draft of a book, there are SO many technical issues that don't make sense.<br /><br />This book is trying to be acomaf… except with the worst parts of Twilight sprinkled into it. First of all, there is such a power imbalance between fae &amp; humans that is emphasized and often exploited. Fae are clever and trick humans and that’s part of the folklore, but for a romantic relationship to exist between the two, it sets up a very manipulative and sketchy dynamic. At one point when he’s mad at her, he pins her to a wall and Isobel is fully aware of her helplessness. It just was an uncomfortable dynamic that I think unwittingly could have been a metaphor for women who can’t help themselves out of abusive relationships. And he constantly holds his age over her head, belittling her with his immortality. At every turn Isobel reminds the reader about how helpless and weak she is as a mere human, and it was exasperating.<br /><br />Next, Isobel falls in love with Rook so!!!!! quickly!!!!!!! I don’t consider this similar to Twilight so much as I consider it a hallmark of any YA novel, but still. The romance in this is SO lame and badly done, too quick, too unbelievable. Her obsession with him not only as a partner but as someone more mysterious and ~better~ than her was really disturbing. She reminded me of Bella because of her meekness, her malleability of character. Also, Rook really does nothing to justify her loving him. It felt very much just like the author stated it but the characters don’t really match up with that description?<br /><br />And that seemed to be something to occur often. For some reason, the plot of this just didn’t work. The best way I can describe is it that the author had the outline of a plot but then filled characters into it that just weren’t right. Their motivations felt off and I felt like I was being tossed back and forth in a tidal wave because their emotions and the direction of the plot kept changing. Bottom line, this wasn’t convincing. And it’s the first book I’ve read in a long time where I think there’s some genuinely weak storytelling here. <br /><br />Furthermore, the characters' words and actions were completely different. She falls in love with him on page 3, yet later on she acts like she's so angry that he's taking her to autumn court? then she wants to escape because she misses her family, but she doesn't want to leave him? again, back to the tidal wave thing. i couldn't figure out any of the characters' motivations, and the world building was just as weakly written, if not worse. nothing made sense. Rook said he was taking her to go on trial at the autumn court, and after like 50 pages of stumbling around the woods, they never even step foot in autumn court once in the book ?????<br /><br />The writing style in this book was also giving me whiplash. Some sentences were so uniquely phrased and vivid, but others rested on clichés i’ve read a thousand times in other YA books. Also sometimes the narration would fall into second person and Isobel would say, “Now let me tell YOU about a time . . .” and it really disrupted the story. It felt very out of place in this sort of story, whereas I may not have minded so much had this been middle grade or contemporary. But something about the breaking of the fourth wall made the story seem tacky, the narrator less real. <br /><br />I’m just a plain sucker for the enemies to lovers trope, but it didn't even deliver on that front. I think it was an ambitious idea, but not at ALL well-executed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15813705542919587680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2202169931">
  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer9779578278141824590"><i>Full review posted</i><br/><br/>It’s really funny because I read this book like 2 weeks ago and I literally remember zero things about it and still haven’t written a review ha ha!! Isn’t this great??!! <s>end me now please</s><br/><br/>So, let’s be direct about it, <b>
  <i>this book was a cringe fest</i>
</b><br/><i>Ahhhhh</i> that felt good to get off my chest. <br/><br/>Now here’s the thing about it, if you go into it with low expectations, expecting a cringe fest with some weirda*s instalove and lots of confusion, then you might be pleasantly surprised bc h</span>
  <span id="freeText9779578278141824590" style="display:none"><i>Full review posted</i><br /><br />It’s really funny because I read this book like 2 weeks ago and I literally remember zero things about it and still haven’t written a review ha ha!! Isn’t this great??!! <s>end me now please</s><br /><br />So, let’s be direct about it, <b>
  <i>this book was a cringe fest</i>
</b><br /><i>Ahhhhh</i> that felt good to get off my chest. <br /><br />Now here’s the thing about it, if you go into it with low expectations, expecting a cringe fest with some weirda*s instalove and lots of confusion, then you might be pleasantly surprised bc hey it’s not //that// bad. Problem for me was, I went in with sky high expectations. ;-; sad<br /><br />Anywho, let’s jot note it out,<br />-	On a positive note <s>bc we all know how much I reek of positivity</s> the world is pretty interesting. It’s magical enough and genuinely captivating with its flowery words<br />-	Really creative plot i.e. the fair folk interact with humans on a professional level as they cannot partake in any human craft – so they hire humans to do it for them (but theyre also evil and mean and ish)<br />-	The mc’s goat sister’s were pretty good too. And I liked the strong family aspect, that’s always my weak spot<br />-	THE MC IS AN ARTIST!!!!<br />-	The fact that it’s a standalone is a bonus for me bc we NEVER get good fantasy standalone and I crave them<br />-	Well….it’s short. So it was easy to binge and be done with :)<br />-	Um…..i think I’ve ran out of positive things to say….<br />-	🙅 the 🙅 cringe 🙅 insta 🙅 love 🙅<br />-	Y’all probably thing im exaggerating but im literally not THEY WERE TALKING ABOUT FALLING IN LOVE AFTER LIKE 3 PARAGRAPHS I WANTED TO CRY<br />-	This quote in itself: <br /><blockquote>
  <i>I automatically tightened my legs around his waist and hooked my arms around his neck, boggling at how high off the ground he’d lifted me. <b>It was almost like riding him as a horse again</b></i>
</blockquote><br />-	Legit choked on air when I heard the narrator read that line, like…..why, why, please stop<br />-	These kids were //pretending// to hate each other AFTER THE WHOLE INSTALOVE TRIP AND I WAS SO CONFUSED BC THEY PRACTICALLY PROCLAIMED THEIR LOVE FOR EACH OTHER WHY THEY LYING SO MUCH<br />-	And then 0.34 seconds later theyre like making out in the woods????<br />-	Dude, try and be consistent, please<br />-	And then some ish happened but I forgot and then the real conflict started but it literally ended in 2 seconds so that’s great<br />-	Moral of the story: punch me if I believe in the hype again, thanks.<br /><br /><i>“Why do we desire, above all other things, that which has the greatest power to destroy us?”</i><br /><br />2 stars!!<br /><br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Buddy read</i>
</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36873117" rel="nofollow noopener">marmoosha</a>  who has already pretty much ditched me. :|<br /><br />This is the FIRST book im doing as part of our <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/409533-the-24-hour-readathon" rel="nofollow noopener">24 Hour Readathon</a> <s>feel free to join the readathon if you please</s></span>

<div id="review_1992925350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1992925350" />
    <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads"><img alt="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549084p2/13699205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1992925350?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ELLIAS (elliasreads)" href="/user/show/13699205-ellias-elliasreads">ELLIAS (elliasreads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=2017-books">2017-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13699205-ellias-elliasreads?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992925350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17929760875923042484"><b>Beautifully written and living up to its own with a unique spin on fairy lore and magic,</b> <i>An Enchantment of Ravens</i>, was simply at best, a <i>short, solid, and an enchanting</i> read. <br/><br/>Full of lush and prose writing, the author takes us on a wondrous journey through a very different take on the fairy world, that stands very well on its own. This book is a standalone so don't worry about any sequels coming afterwards. I, for one though, wouldn't complain if there were other books written within the same un</span>
  <span id="freeText17929760875923042484" style="display:none"><b>Beautifully written and living up to its own with a unique spin on fairy lore and magic,</b> <i>An Enchantment of Ravens</i>, was simply at best, a <i>short, solid, and an enchanting</i> read. <br /><br />Full of lush and prose writing, the author takes us on a wondrous journey through a very different take on the fairy world, that stands very well on its own. This book is a standalone so don't worry about any sequels coming afterwards. I, for one though, wouldn't complain if there were other books written within the same universe. The magic and the world itself was so interesting; I wish the author would have expanded on it just a bit. From the blurb and early reviews I can see that a lot of people might compare this book to, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>. <br /><br />However, skip all the raunchiness and hyphens, you have a better written, well-meaning, and crafted story. <i>(People who've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>, will only get this joke, calm down.)</i><br /><br />However, there were several aspects which I did not like and I will go more in depth with a video on my channel closer to the release date of the book. In short, the middle lagged a bit for me and the ending was very rushed. <br /><br />This book is basically your average fairy tale expanded and glorified with better story, plot, and writing. I think people who have read, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a>, will really <i>really</i> enjoy this book. <br /><br />It's a beautifully composed story: an artsy fairy tale and nothing more. <br /><br /><b>3 ENCHANTING STARS</b><br /><br /><i>Thank you to Simon and Schuster for proving me an arc. All thoughts and opinions are my own.</i><br /><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/branbookaddict" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/brandonthebookaddict/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookstagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/brandonthebookaddict" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> |</span>
  <a data-text-id="17929760875923042484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/wqGbTeUsc7Ekzm/iCh+4gMc2VI4a+cd5LZJFp6z2lFswZq5TWHb/tjhYNzWDH6pd4nZvFYjFNLnWNw+6758Kw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eN95DT/90CMGSSwEBdx43axaabw07wSSfXxkmLNTRb7rFGXZRQi6Exo7dWdb+HiW2M9pUlqn911+kvGwxl7jxA==')})
  }
